\mbox{\Hypertarget{group___decoder_gae3ffaf23301bec85ca0c2c7499f484a3}\label{group___decoder_gae3ffaf23301bec85ca0c2c7499f484a3}} 
\index{Decoders and encoders for different protocols@{Decoders and encoders for different protocols}!sendJVCMSB@{sendJVCMSB}}
\index{sendJVCMSB@{sendJVCMSB}!Decoders and encoders for different protocols@{Decoders and encoders for different protocols}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{sendJVCMSB()}{sendJVCMSB()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void IRsend\+::send\+JVCMSB (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{unsigned long}]{data,  }\item[{int}]{nbits,  }\item[{bool}]{repeat = {\ttfamily false} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

With Send \mbox{\hyperlink{group___decoder_gae3ffaf23301bec85ca0c2c7499f484a3}{send\+JVCMSB()}} you can send your old 32 bit codes. To convert one into the other, you must reverse the byte positions and then reverse all bit positions of each byte. Or write it as one binary string and reverse/mirror it. Example\+: 0x\+CB340102 byte reverse -\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 02 01 34 CB bit reverse-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 40 80 2C D3. 0x\+CB340102 is binary 11001011001101000000000100000010. 0x40802\+CD3 is binary 01000000100000000010110011010011. If you read the first binary sequence backwards (right to left), you get the second sequence.

If you read the first binary sequence backwards (right to left), you get the second sequence.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{group___decoder_ga5174f63b73d3ba9fe997bdb98a4af0c5}\label{group___decoder_ga5174f63b73d3ba9fe997bdb98a4af0c5}} 
\index{Decoders and encoders for different protocols@{Decoders and encoders for different protocols}!sendPronto@{sendPronto}}
\index{sendPronto@{sendPronto}!Decoders and encoders for different protocols@{Decoders and encoders for different protocols}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{sendPronto()}{sendPronto()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void IRsend\+::send\+Pronto (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const char $\ast$}]{str,  }\item[{uint\+\_\+fast8\+\_\+t}]{a\+Number\+Of\+Repeats = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{_i_rremote_int_8h_a5d35fb37031b53f0083f8b88ae3cf2c2}{NO\+\_\+\+REPEATS}}} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Parse the string given as Pronto Hex, and send it a number of times given as the second argument. Thereby the division of the Pronto Hex into an intro-\/sequence and a repeat sequence is taken into account\+: First the intro sequence is sent, then the repeat sequence is sent times-\/1 times. However, if the intro sequence is empty, the repeat sequence is sent times times. \href{http://www.harctoolbox.org/Glossary.html\#ProntoSemantics}{\texttt{ Reference}}.

Note\+: Using this function is very wasteful for the memory consumption on a small board. Normally it is a much better idea to use a tool like e.\+g. Ir\+Scrutinizer to transform Pronto type signals offline to a more memory efficient format.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em str} & C type string (null terminated) containing a Pronto Hex representation. \\
\hline
{\em a\+Number\+Of\+Repeats} & Number of times to send the signal. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
